<p>Your answer would be (d). Here, the correct answer is much longer than the distracters and the student may choose it for that reason only. It has been made too obvious.</p>
<p>Using common mistakes for distracters can be very effective. Here is a good example.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-child-with-fever-has-been-admitted-to-your-health-centre-he-does-not-seem-to-have-any-infection-you-have-given-him-some-chloroquine-what-else-should-you-do">A child with fever has been admitted to your health centre. He does not seem to have any infection. You have given him some chloroquine. What else should you do?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-child-with-fever-has-been-admitted-to-your-health-centre-he-does-not-seem-to-have-any-infection-you-have-given-him-some-chloroquine-what-else-should-you-do" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Answers:</p>
<p>a. Check for dehydration
b. Give antibiotics
c. Refer him to hospital
d. Give aspirin</p>
<p>You will agree that the answers (b), (c) and (d) are all common mistakes made at health centres? The correct response is (a).</p>
<p>You can use MCQs to test different things. Although all MCQs only really test knowledge, you can test different types of knowledge with them. Read the next question, what does it test? Does it simply test what students know about vaccines?</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Your kerosene got finished last week and your refrigerator has not been working. If you get a new supply of kerosene next month and the refrigerator starts working again, your vaccines:</p>
<p>Answers:</p>
<p>a. Will all cause bad reactions
b. Will all be effective
c. Will all be useless
d. Will work again after they have been cold for 24 hours</p>
<p>What does the next question, in contrast, test? Josephine's road-to-health card shows that she was born in December. She has had only one immunisation, the first DPT, given in February. It is now May. What immunisations does she need?</p>
<p>Answer:</p>
<p>a. BCG only.
b. BCG and DPT.
c. BCG, DPT and polio.
d. BCG, DPT, polio &amp; measles.</p>
<p>Your answer should be (c).</p>
<p>You can therefore see that MCQs can be used to test different sorts of knowledge. They can also be used for pre and post test purposes. They would help you gauge how effective your teaching is and determine whether or not the students are learning.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="assessing-skills">Assessing Skills<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessing-skills" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Skills can be assessed through the use of:</p>
<ul>
<li>Objective structured clinical examination (OSCE)</li>
<li>Objective structured practical examination (OSPE)</li>
</ul>
<p>For both methods, candidates pass through a number of examination stations to answers or solve various problems. Questions vary from practical skills, knowledge, application and testing of attitudes. All candidates get the same experience.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objective-structured-practical-examination-ospe">Objective Structured Practical Examination (OSPE)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objective-structured-practical-examination-ospe" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Practical skills are very important components of training in all professions.</p>
<p>Failure in practical tests is equivalent to failure in the whole examination.</p>
<p>You should not allow excellence in theory to compensate for a failure in practicals.</p>
<p>OSPE examinations must be objective, valid and reliable. They should define the competencies a worker needs to develop in order for them to successfully perform the job. This ensures that all examiners have similar expectations.</p>
<p>Look for a correct diagram in a clinical case. Assess the student's skills using rating scales or a checklist. You should set short answers to practical problem solving skills questions to ensure objective assessment. In order to improve the validity of the test, you should increase the sample thus increasing the range of competencies to be tested. Draw up in advance a table of specifications to be tested on.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objective-structured-clinical-examination-osce">Objective Structured Clinical Examination (OSCE)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objective-structured-clinical-examination-osce" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a comprehensive examination of a patient. The student spends 15 to 60 minutes with a patient and then discusses that patient with a panel of examiners (long case). The exam should be set up in the following manner:</p>
<ul>
<li>Brief examination of a patient followed by oral questions (known as viva voce).</li>
<li>Assessment of the learner's actual work during practice using rating scales.</li>
<li>Assessment of log and procedure books.</li>
<li>Case record and case reports.</li>
<li>Models or phantoms.</li>
</ul>
<p>The following are stages of setting an OSPE:</p>
<ul>
<li>Identify topics/competencies to be tested on.</li>
<li>Decide the number of stations and timing.</li>
<li>Allocate topics and competencies to be tested.</li>
<li>Set up instructions for examiners rating scales/check list for each station.</li>
<li>List resources required for each station. These include examiners, markers and observers, patients, normal persons and simulation and room furniture, that is, beds, clocks, bells and so on.</li>
<li>Allocate marks for each station.</li>
<li>Allocate marks within the station, that is, for each item of the question.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Prepare standard/model answers for the questions.</li>
</ul>
<p>The main advantages of OSPE include:</p>
<ul>
<li>OSPE separates the assessment of process and product by ensuring that the student performs the procedure as they are being observed.</li>
<li>Allows adequate sampling of skills.</li>
<li>Allows analytic and objective observation of skills because the observed skill is quite specific.</li>
<li>Can be used as quick feedback for students and teachers, especially before certification, as a revision tool.</li>
</ul>
<p>However, OSPE also has several disadvantages.</p>
<ul>
<li>The process can appear impersonal</li>
<li>It takes time to organise</li>
<li>It can interfere with the provision of other services</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="assessing-attitudes">Assessing Attitudes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessing-attitudes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The student's attitude is an important ingredient in delivering a good service. By assessing this skill, a student will learn the importance of having a good attitude and will understand what is expected of them.</li>
<li>Attitudes can be assessed indirectly, that is, as the candidate performs a skill. This will have to be over a long period so that your assessment is based on repetition of the same attitude over time. Assessing of attitudes should be a continuous process to give a student the chance to internalise the specific attitude.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-do-you-use-to-assess-attitudes">What do you use to assess attitudes?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-do-you-use-to-assess-attitudes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Pencil and paper test questions can be set for knowledge based tests. However, simulations, allowing the observation of gestures and actions, are a better way to see the actual display of attitude.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-tools">Types of Tools<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-tools" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You can use a rating scale based on a table analysis (TA). There are two types of scales:</p>
<ul>
<li>Scale of 5-1. This should remind you of the XY forms you had to have filled in by your ward in charge. A simple satisfactory to unsatisfactory scale is another example.</li>
<li>Semantic differential, that is, a scale on opposite characteristics. This can be used on attitudes alone. One example is given below.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="example">Example:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#example" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Please tick where the student exhibits this behavioural characteristic.</p>
<ul>
<li>Keen and willing â€“ does minimum work.</li>
<li>Accepts instructions â€“ ignores instructions.</li>
<li>Polite to patients â€“ Rude.</li>
</ul>
<p>Set up instructions for examiners' rating scales/check list for each station. List resources required for each station including examiners, markers and observers. Allocate marks for each station and within each station, that is, for each item of the question. Prepare standard or model answers for the questions.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="developing-assessment-tools">Developing Assessment Tools<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#developing-assessment-tools" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You can develop an assessment tool by following these basic steps:</p>
<ul>
<li>List the objectives you wish to evaluate.</li>
<li>Identify the expected learner outcomes (knowledge, attitude and skills).</li>
<li>Specify the tools of assessment such as essays, MCQs, OSPE, and so on.</li>
<li>Allocate marks for each objective and develop a marking scheme.</li>
<li>Construct questions for the whole test.</li>
<li>Arrange questions from the first to the last.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="grading">Grading<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#grading" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This refers to the awarding of marks, score or a value to the assignment performed. Some examples of grading include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Percentage of 0-100%.</li>
<li>Pass or fail, good, average, excellent.</li>
<li>Percentiles.</li>
<li>Letter grades, that is, A, B, C, D, E or F.</li>
</ul>
<p>Valuation of student performance is important. This is mainly because it gauges the extent to which educational objectives have been achieved and guides the teacher in deciding what steps need to be planned next to facilitate learning for the students.</p>
<p>THE END</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="teaching-methodology">TEACHING METHODOLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#teaching-methodology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="main-objective">Main Objective<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#main-objective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>By the end of the unit, the learner should be able to apply the concepts and principles of teaching and learning</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sub-objectives">Sub objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sub-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>By the end of the unit the learner should be able to</li>
<li>Explain the basic concepts and theories of learning</li>
<li>Participate in curriculum development</li>
<li>Develop instructional materials for teaching and learning</li>
<li>Plan, implement and evaluate teaching/learning situation</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="concepts-and-theories-of-learning">Concepts and Theories of learning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#concepts-and-theories-of-learning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<li>Definition of terms</li>
<li>Learning domains/ stages of learning</li>
<li>Factors that influence teaching and learning</li>
<li>Trends in nursing education</li>
<li>Characteristics of a good teacher</li>
<li>Principles and skills used in teaching and learning</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-definition-of-terms">A. Definition of terms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-definition-of-terms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Learning</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A continuous process that results in the acquisition of new behavior pattern through experience or practice</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Teaching</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The act of assisting the learner to modify his behavior through experience, study or intuition. Imparting knowledge</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Learner</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Person acquiring knowledge or skills</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Teacher</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The person who transmits knowledge through personal contact</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Teaching methodology</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Technique used by the teacher to promote learning</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Climate setting</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The process of creating an atmosphere of free interaction between the participants themselves and their facilitators</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="learning">Learning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#learning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A continuous process that alters behavior through training</li>
<li>A learning situation is potentiated through four ingredients</li>
</ul>
<p>a) Motivation
b) Information
c) Practice
d) Feedback</p>
<p>The change in behavior addresses a felt need, which occurs through experience</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="principles-of-learning">Principles of learning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-learning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>What is a principle?</li>
<li>A fact, rule, law about something that occur as a result of repeated experience leading to the deeper understanding of ideas on the processes of teaching and learning</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="principles-of-learning">Principles of learning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-learning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Students learn what is relevant and useful</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When the material is presented in a sequential and logical manner</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Learn when actively involved</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When they receive feedback on their performance</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Conducive environment</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Recognizes peoples right to make mistakes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Encourages openness of mind and trust in self</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Involves practice and repetition</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Speed of presenting and speed at which learners learn match</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Message is clear</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Learners are motivated</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>People learn and remember things that are exciting, dramatic or pleasant more easily than those boring unpleasant things</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="principles-of-adult-learning-andragogy">Principles of adult learning (Andragogy)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-adult-learning-andragogy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Andragogy is the art of helping adults learn while pedagogy is the art of helping children learn.</li>
<li>The principles of adult learning include</li>
<li>It is self directed</li>
<li>The teacher facilitates learning rather than directing it</li>
<li>Adult learners learn best by being active rather than passive</li>
<li>Learning is optimum when the content are applicable immediately to existing problems or their own situations</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="principles-of-andragogy">Principles of andragogy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-andragogy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Adult learners bring with them a wealth of experience</li>
<li>Adult learners can help each other because of their experience, encourage them to do so</li>
<li>The learners should be encouraged to continuously evaluate their learning</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assignment">ASSIGNMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assignment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Outline the principles of pedagogy</li>
<li>Review the trends in nursing education: history of nursing education, influencing factors, challenges and emerging issues</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="what-makes-one-a-better-learner">What makes one a better learner?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-makes-one-a-better-learner" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>â˜‘ Small tutorial groups</li>
<li>â˜‘ Working at own pace</li>
<li>â˜‘ When you know the goals</li>
<li>â˜‘ When motivated by the relevance of the goals</li>
<li>â˜‘ Lively atmosphere</li>
<li>â˜‘ Practicing what has been learnt</li>
<li>â˜‘ When learning will help solve a problem</li>
<li>â˜‘ When exposed to different kinds of stimuli</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="characteristics-of-learning">Characteristics of learning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-learning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>It produces a behavior change in the learner</li>
<li>It leads to a relatively permanent change</li>
<li>It results from practice and repetition of experience</li>
<li>It is directly observant ie, abstract</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="factors-influencing-learning-conditions">Factors influencing learning (conditions)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-influencing-learning-conditions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Maturation/ age
Mature enough to adapt to the expected behavior</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ability potential (intelligence)
One's ability to acquire knowledge and carry out a particular responsibility</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Previous learning experience
Extra coaching needed where there is no previous experience</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Motivation</p>
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Internal and external conditions of learning</li>
</ul>
<ol start="5">
<li>
<p>Level of aspiration</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Physical &amp; emotional state: sickness, fatigue, physical disability</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Psychological state: fear, anxiety, excitement</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Importance of material to the learner</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Participation of the learner: should be actively involved eg asking and answering questions</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Socio economic factors</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Feedback</p>
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Should be given in time to ensure learning takes place</li>
</ul>
<ol start="12">
<li>Learners environment: conducive</li>
<li>Practice and guidance: more improves performance &amp; learning</li>
<li>Methods of teaching</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<ol start="15">
<li>Re enforcement</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>A re enforcer is anything that strengthens behavior and increases the probability of its reoccurrence</li>
<li>Eg attention, recognition, praise, awards, confirmation of the right answer</li>
<li>2 types positive and negative re enforcement</li>
</ul>
<p>Positive encourage positive behavior</p>
<p>Negative discourage unacceptable behavior</p>
<ul>
<li>Components of re enforcement</li>
<li>â˜‘ Verbal: praise, encouragement, feedback</li>
<li>â˜‘ Gestures: nodding, clapping, thumbing</li>
<li>â˜‘ Activity: related to the lesson</li>
<li>â˜‘ Proximity: closeness to the student, physical content, handshake</li>
<li>â˜‘ Token/ rewards</li>
</ul>
<p>NB: Effective re enforcement should be immediate, understandable and meaningful to the student</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="learning-domains-stages-of-learning">Learning Domains (Stages of learning)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#learning-domains-stages-of-learning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Cognitive learning</li>
<li>Psychomotor learning</li>
<li>Affective learning</li>
</ol>
<p>a) Cognitive Learning</p>
<ul>
<li>Relates to recall of knowledge &amp; development of intellectual abilities and skills</li>
<li>Concerned with knowledge of facts, concepts of information, thinking and reasoning</li>
<li>Used in academic studies</li>
<li>Involves 6 levels of knowledge acquisition</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="levels-of-knowledge-acquisition">Levels of knowledge acquisition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#levels-of-knowledge-acquisition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Simple knowledge</li>
<li>Identification</li>
<li>Application</li>
<li>Analysis</li>
<li>Synthesis</li>
<li>Evaluation</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Simple knowledge: recall and memorization of facts. A.k.a discrimination. It is the lowest level of learning.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Verbs used include name, list</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Identification: learner needs to learn more. A.k.a comprehensive level. The learner should be able to recognize, interpret and state different things.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Verbs: describe, classify, identify, indicate</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Application: the ability to use theories or principles in new situations.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Verbs: apply, discuss, determine, illustrate</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Analysis: the ability to divide the complex knowledge into separate parts.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Verbs: analyze, categorize, calculate, differentiate, compare</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Synthesis: the ability to put together separate elements of knowledge and generate principles to form new patterns or a whole component.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Verbs: create, manage, plan, formulate, construct, write a proposal</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Evaluate: the ability to make judgment &amp; make decisions using the acquired knowledge or inform action</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Verbs: evaluate, argue, select</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>b) Psychomotor Learning</p>
<ul>
<li>It involves learning of skills or practical ability.</li>
<li>The skills involve movement thus motor/ psychomotor</li>
<li>Levels in this domain include:</li>
<li>Imitation</li>
<li>Manipulation</li>
<li>Precision</li>
<li>Articulation</li>
<li>Naturalization</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="levels-of-psychomotor-learning">Levels of psychomotor learning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#levels-of-psychomotor-learning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p><strong>Imitation</strong>: the learner is exposed to an observable action at the level of his/her muscular system guided by an impulse to imitate it.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Involves gross body movements</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Manipulation</strong>: learner is prepared for adjustment to a particular action followed by finely coordinated movement</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The learner performs and acts according to instruction</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Precision: a high level performance. There is proficiency in performance to reproduce a given act under instruction and guidance</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Articulation: involves the coordination of a series of acts by establishing an appropriate sequence among different acts, ability to communicate, verbal &amp; non verbal</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Naturalization: skills of performance attains its highest level of proficiency in a single act or a series of articulated acts.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The act is performed with minimal expenditure of energy</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>c) Affective learning</p>
<ul>
<li>Concerned with interest, attitudes &amp; values of people &amp; development of appreciation &amp;adequate adjustment.</li>
<li>In this domain, learners learn to share, argue &amp; cooperate with one another</li>
<li>Certain attitudes are formed or changed through training</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="levels-in-affective-domain">Levels in affective domain<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#levels-in-affective-domain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Receiving: willingness to pay attention to the information</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Responding: willingness to accept an event through some form of participation. Learner shows interest to what is happening</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Valuing: willingness to accept an event through expression of positive attitude</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Organization: the learner meets the situation of which more than one value is relevant.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Characterization: the learner consistently acts in accordance with the value s/he accepts &amp; incorporates this behavior as part of their personality</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="how-learning-takes-place">How learning takes place<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-learning-takes-place" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Through reasoning, getting facts, organizing &amp; choosing the best alternative</li>
<li>Can take place in the absence of the teacher</li>
<li>In a learning situation the teacher is the facilitator</li>
<li>Learning can be formal or informal</li>
<li>Learning takes time</li>
<li>Attitudes and values are developed through observation</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="theories-of-learning">THEORIES OF LEARNING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#theories-of-learning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>What is a theory?</li>
<li>Refers to an idea used to account for a situation or justify a course of action</li>
<li>A set of principles on which the practice of an activity is based</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-main-learning-theories">3 Main Learning Theories<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-main-learning-theories" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Cognitive theories</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Behaviorist theories</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Humanistic/ social psychologist</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Behaviorist theories</p>
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>B.F. Skinner: operant conditioning</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>suggests that learning will occur if behavior is followed by pleasant consequences.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Look Skinner box experiment</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>He introduced the law of effect thus reinforcement</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The teacher determines the direction of learning depending on the kind of reward</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The theory elicits 3 kinds of responses:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Neutral operands:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Reinforcers</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Punishers</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="thorndike-theory">Thorndike theory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#thorndike-theory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Proposed that learning is more meaningful when the outcome is made clear.</li>
<li>Learning occurs by creating associations between stimuli and responses</li>
<li>Transfer of learning depends on the presence of identical elements in the original &amp; new learning situations.</li>
<li>These should be specific, not general</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ivan-pavlov-theory">Ivan Pavlov Theory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ivan-pavlov-theory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Classical conditioning</li>
<li>Reinforcement and punishment</li>
<li>Automatic responses</li>
<li>Association between the stimuli to produce certain responses</li>
<li>Learning to associate unconditioned stimuli UCS that results in a certain unconditioned response UCR, with a conditioned stimuli CS, such that the new stimuli brings about same effect</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="watson-theory">Watson theory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#watson-theory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Emphasized active participation in learning or learning by practice</li>
<li>A child's behavior is influenced by their environment rather than their genetic makeup or natural temperament</li>
<li>Little Albert's experiment</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-cognitive-theories">2. Cognitive Theories<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-cognitive-theories" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>B S Bloom theory</li>
<li>3 domains of learning</li>
<li>Affective, cognitive, psychomotor</li>
<li>Outlines levels of learning in each domain from basic to complex</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="d-p-ausubel-theory">D P Ausubel theory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#d-p-ausubel-theory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Proposed that theory is the basis for practice of beginning with learners existing knowledge</li>
<li>Learning is related to learners knowledge base before new content is presented</li>
<li>New material is an extension of what is already known</li>
</ul>
<p>J.BRUNNER</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>He recommended that learns should be encouraged to work out things for themselves.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Learner should relate new material to pre existing knowledge and deduce a meaning</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Aim of education should be to create an autonomous learner</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Learning to learn</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Teacher facilitates thinking and imparts problem solving skills</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Discovery learning</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Learners have goals and are provided with resources that allows them to work out solutions too their problems through own effort and use of appropriate resources</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="humanistic-social-psychologist">HUMANISTIC/SOCIAL PSYCHOLOGIST<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#humanistic-social-psychologist" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>CARL ROGERS&gt; Learner centered approach to learning</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>His main propositions included:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>All humans have a natural potential and desire to learn</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Learning occurs when the learner perceives relevance related to their own purpose</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Significant learning is through doing</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Learner chooses their direction discovers resources and formulates problems</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Most learning is self initiated and involves the whole person</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Self evaluation is key in effective mature learning</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Learners should retain a continuing openness to change</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The theory contributed to adult learning principles</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It emphasizes use of small group discussion</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The teacher is guide/facilitator</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rogers philosophy</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="abraham-maslow-theory">ABRAHAM MASLOW THEORY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#abraham-maslow-theory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>He encouraged the need to focus on the development of the student as a person with a role in the society</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Self knowledge: one develops a set of values to guide them through life</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Learning for self enhancement rather than for utility</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Learning out of interest than to gain more qualifications</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Individual decides what to learn and how to learn it</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Social learning theory is based upon the work of Albert Bandura. It is also referred to as Social Cognitive Theory (SCT)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This theory attempts to understand the process that is involved in explaining how we learn from each other</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It focuses on learning that occurs by <strong>direct experience</strong> by observing, imitating, and modeling</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It provides a framework for understanding, predicting and potentially changing human behaviour.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Aspects of Banduraâ€™s theory are that:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>children learn by observing others,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>the same set of stimuli may provoke different responses from different people, or from the same people at different times</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>the environment and a personâ€™s behaviour are interlinked;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>personality is an interaction between three factors: the environment, behaviour, and a personâ€™s psychological processes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>All 3 play an important role in the learning process. They are constantly influencing each other</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Environmental factors would include</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Social aspects - peers, family and teachers and Physical factors - the layout or size of the class room or the temperature of the room</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="implications-in-classroom">Implications in classroom<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#implications-in-classroom" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Social learning theory has numerous implications for classroom use. The theory revolves around the notion that learning correlates to the observation of role models. In education, for example, teachers play the role of a model in a child's learning acquisition.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Students often learn a great deal simply by observing other people.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Describing the consequences of behavior can effectively increase the appropriate behaviors and decrease inappropriate ones. Discussing with learners about the rewards and consequences of various behaviors.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Teachers and parents must model appropriate behaviors and take care that they do not model inappropriate behaviors.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Describing the consequences of behavior can effectively increase the appropriate behaviors and decrease inappropriate ones. Discussing with learners about the rewards and consequences of various behaviors.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Teachers and parents must model appropriate behaviors and take care that they do not model inappropriate behaviors.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Effective modelling teaches general rules and strategies for dealing with different situations. Teachers should model the behaviors and cognitive processes they want students to learn. Effective instruction, moreover, should include multiple types of models (e.g., teacher, peers, parents) and various forms of modeling (e.g. cognitive, verbal, mastery, coping).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>goal setting is another central process within SCT (Bandura, 1986; Schunk, 1990). Goals reflect cognitive representations of anticipated, desired, or preferred outcomes. Hence, goals exemplify the agency view within SCT that people not only learn, they use forethought to envision the future, identify desired outcomes, and generate plans of action</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In practice this theory will involve:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>children working together on collaborative tasks</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>the less able working with more able children</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>teacher demonstrations</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>peer support</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="principles-of-teaching">PRINCIPLES OF TEACHING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-teaching" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Teaching is assisting the learner to modify his behavior through training or experience</li>
<li>Purpose of teaching: help learner to
a) Acquire, retain and utilize the knowledge
b) Acquire skills
c) Establish habits and develop attitudes
d) Understand, analyze, synthesize and evaluate the knowledge</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="characteristics-of-a-good-teacher">CHARACTERISTICS OF A GOOD TEACHER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-a-good-teacher" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Warmth</li>
<li>Cognitive organization</li>
<li>Orderliness</li>
<li>Indirectness</li>
<li>Ability to solve instructional problems</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Warmth&gt; emotional support, praise and encourage the learner</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cognitive organization&gt; aims learner to acquire understanding/ meaning not memorize.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>presents ideas in a logical sequential manner</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Assesses learners capability to learn, factors in slow learners</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Orderliness&gt; should be systematic and methodical</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Indirectness&gt; learning are indirectly involved through active participation. Self discovery is key in the learning process</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ability to solve instructional problems&gt;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The ability to provide solutions to problems encountered in the teaching/learning situation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Includes technical problems eg poor performance, managerial problems</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="general-principles-of-teaching">General principles of teaching<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-principles-of-teaching" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The teacher helps students learn through:</li>
<li>â˜ Active learning: involve them and give feedback</li>
<li>â˜ Clarity: your teaching should be clear, speak loudly, write neatly and use visual aids</li>
<li>â˜ Ensure mastery: check that all students know and can do it</li>
<li>â˜ Individualize: allow for individual differences and abilities, vary your teaching methods</li>
<li>â˜ Motivation: make teaching interesting, relevant and rewarding</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="active-learning">Active learning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#active-learning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>You can do this in many ways</li>
<li>Give students activities to perform</li>
<li>Ask questions</li>
<li>Set problems or projects</li>
<li>Give feedback or tell them how they could have done better</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-tasks-of-a-teacher">The tasks of a teacher<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-tasks-of-a-teacher" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>6, which include:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Planning</li>
<li>Communication</li>
<li>Providing resources</li>
<li>Counselling</li>
<li>Assessment</li>
<li>Continuing self education</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-planning">1. PLANNING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-planning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Decide what the students should learn, eg by preparing learning objectives</li>
<li>Put content in a suitable sequence</li>
<li>Allocate amounts of time to different learning activities</li>
<li>Select appropriate learning activities and teaching method</li>
<li>Choose assessment procedures: evaluation methods</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-communication">2.COMMUNICATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Ineffective teachers communication leads to ineffective learning</li>
<li>Ways to promote effective communication</li>
<li>Explaining to and advising the learner</li>
<li>Helping the learner to exchange ideas</li>
<li>Provoking the learners to think</li>
<li>Using varied teaching methods</li>
<li>Evaluating whether the learners understand or not and taking necessary measures</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-providing-resources">3. PROVIDING RESOURCES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-providing-resources" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Adequate resources must be provided to ensure effective teaching/learning. These should be obtained prior to teaching</li>
<li>A teacher ensures availability of resources by:</li>
<li>Requesting all required resources in advance</li>
<li>Preparing, selecting or adapting educational materials for the session</li>
<li>Arranging learning experiences especially those that provide opportunities to practice skills eg field visits</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="resources">Resources<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#resources" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Arranging for learners attachments and projects</li>
<li>Involving other health service personnel in teaching the learner</li>
<li>Arranging access to materials eg libraries</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>COUNSELING</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Teaching and learning can be difficult for both teacher and learner thus, the teacher ought to be supportive to the learner</li>
<li>This can be achieved by:</li>
<li>Showing the learners that you care</li>
<li>Listening and attempting to understand the learner</li>
<li>Helping the learner to identify his/her options so as to make decisions</li>
<li>Providing advice and information that is useful to learners</li>
</ul>
<ol start="5">
<li>ASSESSMENT</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Design an assessment that measures how much students have learnt</li>
<li>Use the assessment to guide students learning</li>
<li>Use the assessment to give feedback that modifies teaching</li>
<li>Use the assessment to decide whether your learner is competent to provide healthcare</li>
<li>Encourage the learner to do self evaluation and assess others</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="6-continuing-self-education">6. CONTINUING SELF EDUCATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-continuing-self-education" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Continuing education is vital for all health professionals because of rapid increase in knowledge and technological changes is today's world</li>
<li>The learner perceives the teacher as a resource for information, skills and advice</li>
<li>Thus the teacher should stay informed through self education</li>
</ul>
<p>Ctt...</p>
<ul>
<li>Therefore the teacher should:</li>
<li>Know the subject matter that should be taught &amp; where to find relevant information</li>
<li>Know healthcare delivery systems &amp; any other relevant resources that are available locally</li>
<li>Learners should view the teacher as a model for continuing learning</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="skills-used-in-teaching">Skills used in teaching<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#skills-used-in-teaching" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Setting the audience&gt; introduce the topic, state the objectives to be covered</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Stimulus variation&gt; movement, gestures, focus on the important points, tonal variation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Re enforcement&gt; verbal or non verbal reinforcement</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Basic questioning&gt; distribute questions</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Appropriateness&gt; based on objective and level of learners</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Explanations&gt; clarity and fluency of language, key points noted</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Paraphrasing on the main points&gt; put points in different ways while maintaining same meaning</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Giving examples&gt;give examples within the range of learners knowledge and experience</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Emphasis&gt; use of voice, vary pitch, volume, repeat main points</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Closure of the topic&gt; summarize major points, state relevance and usefulness to the learner</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="balance-between-theory-and-practice">BALANCE BETWEEN THEORY AND PRACTICE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#balance-between-theory-and-practice" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The teacher should strive to maintain a balance between theory and practice</li>
<li>Give more time to teaching rather than learning</li>
<li>Skills are best learnt through practice</li>
<li>Practical sessions need more time to reinforce skill learning and application of theory to practice</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="methods-of-teaching">METHODS OF TEACHING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-of-teaching" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>These methods are chosen prior to the teaching session</li>
<li>Varying the teaching strategies assist learning process.</li>
<li>The methods are divided into 2 kinds&gt;</li>
<li>Traditional teaching methods</li>
<li>Innovative teaching methods</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="traditional-vs-innovative">Traditional Vs Innovative<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#traditional-vs-innovative" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Traditional: the emphasis is in the teacher and how he or she facilitates learning for the students</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Innovative: the focus shifts to the learner while the teachers role is to facilitate learning</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The teacher must define area to be taught, define the subject and topic to be learnt, the objectives and content from the curriculum</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In innovative teaching, the teacher develops tutorial problems which will be used to guide achievement of objectives stated in the curriculum</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The teacher also produces a booklet containing the problems, as they will be used in teaching the course</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Also develops a tutor guide to be used by the facilitator for the course, which must contain solutions and useful tips for guiding the learner</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Innovative learning processes are best described after the tutorial booklet and tutor guide have been developed</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Once these are developed, a tutor can then carry a copy of the booklets for each learner and his own and tutor guide to his tutorial room</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>These processes are difficult during preparation but easy during tutorials and actual course delivery</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-innovative-teaching-methods">Types of innovative teaching methods<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-innovative-teaching-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<ol>
<li>problem based learning PBL</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="2">
<li>self directed learning SDL</li>
</ol>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="teaching-methods">Teaching methods<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#teaching-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Lecture</li>
<li>Discussion</li>
<li>Demonstration</li>
<li>Simulation</li>
<li>Role play</li>
<li>Practical</li>
<li>Field visits</li>
<li>Independent study projects</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<ol start="9">
<li>Seminars</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="10">
<li>Tutorial</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="11">
<li>Project</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="12">
<li>Critical incident technique</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="13">
<li>Team teaching</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="14">
<li>Case study</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<p>LECTURE:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A lesson given orally by the teacher, with no student participation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Content may be distributed in printed form</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Traditional method</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Indications</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Introducing new topic</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Large audience</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Introducing facts</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Limited time</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-discussion">2. DISCUSSION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-discussion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Two way exchange of information, ideas, and feelings between the teacher and the learners</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="methods-include">Methods include<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-include" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>I. Small group discussion
II. Question and answer
III. Syndicate discussion
IV. Debate and panel
V. Snowball discussion
VI. Brainstorming</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Small group discussion:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Teacher divides a class in small groups, gives tasks and facilitates learning</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Question and answer:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Introduction of the topic, what do the learners already know</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Review of learning experience eg field visit</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Informal revision of knowledge, discuss controversial issue</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Syndicate discussion:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A class is divided into several groups. Each group prepares a different assignment and report back to the whole class.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Used to cover wide area of study</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Learners working on common surveys</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Debate and panels:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When working with controversial topics</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Debates: the teacher controls the activity ensures arguments are based on facts</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Panels: several students prepare a topic and present it to class, who then ask the panel questions</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Snowball discussion:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Every single person is involved in the discussion</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Each learner practices the facts to consider, uses these factors to make a decision and listen to other peoples arguments</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Aka pyramidal group discussion</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Brainstorming:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A method of collecting ideas from individual members of a group on how to solve a problem</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Useful in generation of ideas</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Demonstration</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Refers to an inhibition/experiment/explanation of procedures involving practical skills</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Evaluated through return demonstration</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Indications for demonstration</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To reinforce learning</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To show desired performance</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ensures active participation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To help students comprehend and learn information/facts</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To provide practical example as reinforcement for practical work</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Used to illustrate certain attitudes involved in skills</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Simulation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A dynamic representation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An imitation of real life situation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Used to teach attitudes</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="role-play">Role play<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#role-play" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Learner experiences or relives an event</p>
<p>Used to teach communication skills, decision making skills and attitude</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Practical:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Involves learners learning in their future working areas</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Field work/ visits</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Students leave the training school to do the work for which they are trained for</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Mainly observational</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Reinforces knowledge gained in class to a meaningful learning experience</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Independent study project:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A process in which the individual takes the initiative with or without the help of others in diagnosing their learning needs, formulates learning goals, identifies learning resources, chooses and implements appropriate learning strategies and evaluation outcomes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Occurs in 2 forms:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A requirement in a program</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Motivated by learners needs</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="characteristics-of-isp">Characteristics of ISP<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-isp" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Learning objectives are identified by either the learner or the teacher</li>
<li>Involves active student participation</li>
<li>There is use of variety of human and material resources</li>
<li>Individual pacing level of achievement varies</li>
<li>Feedback device is put in place so that the teacher/learner can monitor progress</li>
<li>The is high degree of student autonomy</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Seminar:</li>
<li>A session headed by the teacher, trained senior student or an enthusiastic student fro the class where an assigned subject is discussed.</li>
<li>The subject is prepared prior to the class session and presented by different students.</li>
<li>Other students discuss, criticize and comment on the material presented</li>
</ul>
<p>Tutorial:</p>
<ul>
<li>This is a discussion between a teacher and a small number of students</li>
<li>The smaller the number of students the more effective the tutorial, should not be more than 8</li>
<li>The teacher should do less talking and encourage the students to think and learn independently.</li>
</ul>
<p>PROJECT:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>An assignment is given to an individual student, a pair of orgroup of students in which they carry out a piece of independent work on a particular topic.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The students organize the assignment and prepare a written report to submit to the teacher.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Specified duration for the assignment is given eg within a week or a month</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>CRITICAL INCIDENT TECHNIQUE</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The learner learns from a critical incident which occurs in the course of study of work due to the alarm he/she learns to depict future occurrence</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Eg a health inspector who passes diseased meat as safe for human consumption thus affecting customers</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>TEAM TEACHING:</p>
</li>
<li>
