<p>It is a cooperative approach to teaching where 2 or more teachers take part in planning, teaching and evaluating a group of students.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It improves the quality of instruction by giving teachers opportunity to learn from other team members</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Factors to consider</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Objectives of the session</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Student expectation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Learning activities</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Teachers capabilities</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Content to be covered</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>team teaching</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Guidelines to be considered include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Team members should participate</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Contribution of different ideas</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Carrying out teaching functions in the presence of their colleagues</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Periodic evaluation</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="case-history-studies">Case history/studies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#case-history-studies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>More less the same concept</li>
<li>Case history refers to patient while case studies refer to situations</li>
<li>Case studies describe what happened in a specific situation eg how a specific HIV/AIDS control program was planned and implemented and what the results were</li>
<li>Case history describes a specific part eg presenting symptoms, pmshx,dx, investigations, rx and outcome</li>
<li>Both forms provide useful examples to illustrate general principles</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="micro-teaching-skills">MICRO TEACHING SKILLS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#micro-teaching-skills" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Refer to skills used in the implementation of a good lesson plan in the traditional teaching process</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Include:
i. Set induction
ii. Stimulus variation
iii. Questioning
iv. Re enforcement
v. Use of examples and explanation
vi. Closer/summary</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Set induction: introduce the topic, start a lesson to capture learners attention</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Stimulus variation: varying focus movement, speech and content delivery to retain learners attention</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Questioning: ask questions to promote interaction with the learners and to hold attention</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Re enforcement: reward students to provide good behavior and attention</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Use of examples and explanations: these promote learning</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Closer/summary: mental closure of the lesson.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="lesson-plan">LESSON PLAN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lesson-plan" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This is a written description used in a teaching/learning situation to guide the teacher to systematically present the subject matter in a logical, interrelated and integrated manner such that learning is reinforced and enhanced.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="purpose-of-a-lesson-plan">Purpose of a lesson plan<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#purpose-of-a-lesson-plan" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Helps the teacher to know the topic to teach</li>
<li>Helps the teacher in setting objectives to be taught</li>
<li>Assists the facilitator to plan ahead of time to avoid disorderliness</li>
<li>Enhances systematic flow of information or event</li>
<li>Enables the facilitator to check if the set objectives have been met</li>
<li>Helps in self assessment of the facilitator and allows room for improvement or correction</li>
<li>Helps in outcome of learning</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="contents-of-a-lesson-plan">Contents of a lesson plan<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contents-of-a-lesson-plan" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Topic and specific objectives</li>
<li>Date</li>
<li>Time</li>
<li>Venue</li>
<li>teaching/learning method</li>
<li>Audience</li>
<li>Teaching aid</li>
<li>Institution</li>
<li>Evaluation</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="innovative-teaching-methods">INNOVATIVE TEACHING METHODS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#innovative-teaching-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>In traditional teaching/learning processes, the emphasis is on the teacher &amp; how he/she facilitates learning for the students.</p>
<ul>
<li>In innovative educational processes, the burden of learning shifts to the learner. The teacher is transformed into a facilitator.</li>
<li>In the innovative teaching/learning process, the teacher, like in the traditional process,</li>
<li>must identify the area to be taught,</li>
<li>define the subject &amp; topic to be learnt as well as the objectives&amp; content to be learnt from a curriculum.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="innovative-teaching-methods">INNOVATIVE TEACHING METHODS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#innovative-teaching-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>They include:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Problem Based Learning(PBL)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Self Directed Learning(SDL)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Small Group Tutorial (SGT)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Community Based Education &amp; Service(COBES)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Computer Aided Education (CAE)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Student-centered, Problem based, Integrated, Community-oriented, Electives &amp; Systematic (SPICES)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Of all the above innovative methods, the best known is PBL</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>For innovative teaching/learning methods such as Problem Based Learning(PBL), the teacher must then develop tutorial problems which will be used to guide the achievement of the objectives as stated in the curriculum.</p>
<p>The teacher will also produce a booklet, which contains those problems, as they will be used in teaching the course.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>In addition, the teacher will also develop a tutor guide to be used by the facilitator for the course, which must contain the solutions &amp; useful tips for guiding the learner.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Innovative learning processes are best described after the tutorial booklet &amp; tutor guide have been developed.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>After this have been developed, a tutor can then carry a copy of the booklets for each of his students &amp; his own booklet&amp; tutor guide to his tutorial room.</p>
<ul>
<li>Innovative processes are, therefore, more difficult during preparation but easier during tutorials &amp; actual course delivery</li>
<li>Inside his tutorial room with his group of students, the tutor can follow any one of the following processes to conduct his tutorial</li>
</ul>
<p>The 3 steps Problem Based Learning(PBL)Tutorial(ABC Process)</p>
<p>STEP 1-Tutorial 1</p>
<ul>
<li>Read through the problem, define terms, clarify concept, analyse problem &amp; set learning objectives.</li>
<li>Solve any problem (if possible at this point) eg. on Monday.</li>
<li>Students identify their own learning objectives(SOLO)</li>
</ul>
<p>STEP 2-SDL</p>
<ul>
<li>Self-Directed Learning means that the students study &amp; look for information on their own.</li>
<li>They may do this on Tuesday, Wednesday &amp; Thursday in preparation for the tutorial session on Friday</li>
</ul>
<p>STEP 3-Tutorial 2</p>
<ul>
<li>This is the second tutorial during which students do presentation of gathered information, solution of problems &amp; synthesis.</li>
</ul>
<p>This would take place on a Friday</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-seven-step-pbl-tutorial-process">The Seven Step PBL Tutorial Process<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-seven-step-pbl-tutorial-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>STEP 1: Clarify terms &amp; concepts not readily comprehensible</li>
<li>STEP 2: Define the problem</li>
<li>STEP 3: Analyse the problem</li>
<li>STEP 4: Draw a systematic inventory of the explanations inferred in step 3</li>
<li>STEP 5: Formulate learning objectives</li>
<li>STEP 6: Collect additional information outside the group (SDL)</li>
<li>STEP 7: Synthesize &amp; test the newly acquired information</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-10-step-pbl-tutorial-process">The 10-step PBL Tutorial Process<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-10-step-pbl-tutorial-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>STEP 1 to STEP 7: Similar to the 7 steps PBL Tutorial process</li>
<li>STEP 8: Meet as groups to draw inventory of unresolved issues</li>
<li>STEP 9: Second Self-Directed Learning</li>
<li>STEP 10: Meet again &amp; synthesize the newly acquired information</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-15-step-pbl-tutorial-process">The 15-step PBL Tutorial Process<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-15-step-pbl-tutorial-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Was developed at Moi University Faculty of Health Sciences</p>
<p><strong>First Tutorial</strong></p>
<p>STEP 1: Group organization: Introductions
: Selection of chairman
: Selection of secretary</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>STEP 2: Reading through the problem (aloud)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>STEP 3: Identifying the problem</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>STEP 4: Defining the problem</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>STEP 5: Raising learning issues</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>STEP 6: Resolving issues based on prior knowledge</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>STEP 7: Organization of the unresolved issues</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>STEP 8: Developing learning objectives from the organized unresolved issues</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="first-self-directed-learning-sdl">First Self-Directed Learning(SDL)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#first-self-directed-learning-sdl" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>STEP 9: Information gathering from all available resources</li>
<li>STEP 10: Students meeting alone under their chairman to collate information &amp; identify the objectives based on information that is so far not available</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="second-tutorial">Second Tutorial<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#second-tutorial" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>STEP 11: Discussion of available information to check for correctness &amp; completeness</li>
<li>STEP 12: Identification of objectives so far not addressed with a view to identifying the resources from which to obtain information.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="second-sdl-period-usually-saturday-sunday">Second SDL Period (usually Saturday &amp; Sunday)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#second-sdl-period-usually-saturday-sunday" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>STEP 13: Information gathering on difficult objectives</li>
<li>STEP 14: Final collation of information &amp; solving of the problem (students meeting alone under their chairman)</li>
<li>STEP 15: Identifying areas that are difficult to understand &amp; seeking help, e.g. overview (if necessary) or seminar</li>
</ul>
<p>NOTE&gt;</p>
<ul>
<li>Of all these various processes, the major steps are encompassed in the 3 step process.</li>
<li>This simply presents a problem to the learner, gives him/her time to do self-directed study &amp; enables him to discover &amp; present his/her solutions.</li>
<li>All this is done with the help of the tutor.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="super-skills-of-innovative-education">SUPER SKILLS OF INNOVATIVE EDUCATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#super-skills-of-innovative-education" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>These are modern innovative teaching / learning skills &amp; are most appropriate for adult learners.</p>
<ul>
<li>Super skills, which bear the acronym <strong>FAGIPW</strong>, emphasize that a tutor ought to:</li>
<li>Facilitate</li>
<li>Advice</li>
<li>Guide</li>
<li>Inform</li>
<li>Participate</li>
<li>Withdraw</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="tutorial-problem-in-pbl">Tutorial Problem In PBL<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tutorial-problem-in-pbl" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>In PBL, a problem may mean any of the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>A problem that is clinical, theoretical, research-based or related to real life</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An idea</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A situation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An event</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An outbreak of disease/disaster</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A newspaper cutting</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A list of objectives</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Innovative methods are often used in combination with other methods to facilitate student learning.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Learning skills developed from innovative teaching methods</p>
<ul>
<li>Communication skills</li>
<li>Problem solving skills</li>
<li>Clinical reasoning skills</li>
<li>Self directed learning skills</li>
<li>Emotional/social support skills Thinking skills</li>
<li>Team-work</li>
<li>Continuing education skills</li>
</ul>
<p>The disadvantages of innovative educational methods are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Their resource-intensive nature</li>
<li>The need to have many tutorial rooms to accommodate the small groups of students instead of the traditional huge lecture hall.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-role-of-the-tutor-in-the-pbl-process">The Role of the Tutor in the PBL Process<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-role-of-the-tutor-in-the-pbl-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>In the innovative teaching/learning processes, the tutor plays as many roles &amp; even more roles than the teachers in the traditional teaching methods.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Establishing rapport</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Explaining goals, objectives &amp; functions</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Explaining procedures &amp; roles of students &amp; tutor in PBL</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Focusing attention</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Encouraging active participation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Referring back questions, comments, suggestions to group</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Intervening in conflict situations</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Reinforcing group discussions</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Control group</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Distribute &amp; re-direct questions</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Probe further, if necessary</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Encourage analysis, synthesis &amp; evaluation of problem(data)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Encourage students to develop qualities of individuals in group</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Intervene to keep group&amp; discussion on track &amp; stimulate thinking by encouraging hypothesizing</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Encourage students to review&amp; redefine explanations</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-role-of-the-student-in-the-pbl-process">The Role of the student in the PBL Process<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-role-of-the-student-in-the-pbl-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Active participation ie. listening, contribution to the discussion &amp; asking questions</li>
<li>Carrying out analysis, synthesis&amp; evaluation of the whole learning process</li>
<li>Making connections, linking concepts &amp; applying principles</li>
<li>Reviewing &amp; redefining explanations</li>
<li>Evaluating achievements</li>
<li>Summarizing at various stages</li>
<li>Acting as change agent, ie, as a solution giver, process helper, resource linker &amp; catalyst</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-teaching">CLINICAL TEACHING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-teaching" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Clinical teaching is teaching in the clinical or practical setting, similar to the environment within which the learner will practice in future.</p>
<ul>
<li>In clinical teaching, you want your learner to put the knowledge of a task or skill into action</li>
<li>You want your student to get involved with the patient/client</li>
<li>Involvement brings in emotions &amp; feelings</li>
</ul>
<p>Ct...</p>
<p>You must teach the learner to emphasize so that he/she can nurture or care without getting carried away by the effects of the illness or situation</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>No learning can take place until certain basic needs of the learner have been met</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When the basic needs get fulfilled, your learner will want to learn at a higher level&amp; exercise mastery of the skills.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Ct...</p>
<p>As the learner carries out procedures, she/he needs to learn how to contain personal negative feelings eg. contempt, revulsion of unpleasant sights or aversion</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Above all, the learner must learn how to maintain his/her integrity &amp; the professional code of ethics &amp; etiquette</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This is necessary because the student will be learning how to protect his/her patient/client from malpractice &amp; negligence</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Mastery of the theory is important because it gives you the foundation</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Scientific knowledge adds appropriate technical skills &amp; encourages you to develop the right attitudes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The result is the development of sound clinical judgement, which is the sign of an experienced nurse.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="role-of-a-clinical-teacher-instructor">Role of a Clinical teacher/ instructor<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#role-of-a-clinical-teacher-instructor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>As a clinical teacher, you should be:</p>
<p>I. A skilled, experienced nurse concerned with the maintenance &amp; improvement of standards of patient care
II. Concerned to help your learner to develop his/her potential as a nurse
III. Able to gain satisfaction from caring for patients</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="role-of-a-clinical-teacher">Role of a clinical teacher<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#role-of-a-clinical-teacher" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>IV. Able to gain satisfaction from teaching, especially individuals &amp; small groups</p>
<p>V. Keen to create a favorable environment for learning.</p>
<p>VI. Alert to the opportunities available for facilitating learning in the clinical situation</p>
<p>VII. A model for your learner</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="factors-to-consider-when-choosing-a-teaching-method">Factors to consider when choosing a teaching method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-to-consider-when-choosing-a-teaching-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<ol>
<li>Teaching/ learning objectives</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<p>What do you want the students to be able to do at the end of the session?</p>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="2">
<li>Practicality of the method</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<p>How much time is needed? Where is the teaching taking place? Number of students involved, level of the students?</p>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="3">
<li>Resources needed</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<p>Gather resources early enough and make the sessions interesting for learning to take place</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="attitudes-knowledge-and-skills">ATTITUDES, KNOWLEDGE AND SKILLS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#attitudes-knowledge-and-skills" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>HOW ATTITUDES ARE TAUGHT</li>
<li>An attitude is a tendency to behave or think in a certain way</li>
<li>Methods of teaching attitudes</li>
<li>Providing information to shape attitudes: films, lectures</li>
<li>Providing examples: model</li>
<li>Providing experience to shape attitudes</li>
<li>Providing discussion to shape attitudes</li>
<li>Role play exercise</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="how-skills-are-taught">HOW SKILLS ARE TAUGHT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-skills-are-taught" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>There are 3 types of skills:</li>
<li>Communication skills: persuading, talking, encouraging</li>
<li>Cognitive skills: thinking, decision making</li>
<li>Psychomotor skills: practical skills, involve movement. Using hands</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="methods-of-teaching-skills">Methods of teaching skills<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-of-teaching-skills" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Describing a skill &gt; explain the rationale and stages in performing it</li>
<li>Demonstrate a skill&gt; students see an expert performing the skill correctly with an explanation of what s/he is doing</li>
<li>Practice&gt; students should perform skills through projects, simulations, ward rotations and case studies</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="how-knowledge-is-taught">HOW KNOWLEDGE IS TAUGHT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-knowledge-is-taught" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It includes the facts that a health worker must know.</p>
<p>Sources of facts include teachers, manuals, books, models, posters</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="methods-for-teaching-knowledge">Methods for teaching knowledge<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-for-teaching-knowledge" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Lecture</li>
<li>Symposium</li>
<li>Seminar</li>
<li>Conference</li>
<li>Panel</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="educational-objectives">EDUCATIONAL OBJECTIVES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#educational-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>What is an Objective?</li>
<li>It is a precise statement that answers the question of what a student should do in order to show that s/he has learnt what the teacher want him/her to learn from the session.</li>
<li>it is a statement describing an instructional outcome</li>
<li>Objectives enable the teacher to help the learner gain the knowledge, skill or attitude specified</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-objectives">Types of objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>A) Instructional objective (practical performance)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>These describe what the learners and the teacher intend to achieve as a result of instruction</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It includes the three domains ie cognitive, affective and psychomotor</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>B) Educational objectives</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>State clear, simple, precise and observable behavior</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Ct...</p>
<ul>
<li>C) Behavioral objectives</li>
<li>They state the actual behavior to be performed, the condition under which it will be performed, the result of the performance and the criteria that will be used to evaluate the product of the performance</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="purpose-of-objectives">Purpose of objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#purpose-of-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Guides the teacher and the learner to remain focused</li>
<li>Helps in keeping to the scope of study</li>
<li>Helps the teacher to be systematic</li>
<li>Influences self directed learning</li>
<li>Allows the teacher/learner to understand the subject with greater clarity</li>
<li>Predetermines the expected outcomes for students</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="characteristics-of-objectives">CHARACTERISTICS OF OBJECTIVES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The objectives should be SMART</li>
<li>S-smart</li>
<li>M-measurable</li>
<li>A-attainable/achievable</li>
<li>R- realistic</li>
<li>T-time bound</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="qualities-of-good-objectives">QUALITIES OF GOOD OBJECTIVES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#qualities-of-good-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>RELEVANCE&gt; most essential to the health needs of a community</li>
<li>CONSISTENT&gt; provides the same meaning / result each time</li>
<li>UNEQUIVOCAL&gt; no argument / dispute about the meaning</li>
<li>FEASIBLE&gt; can be attained or performed</li>
<li>OBSERVABLE&gt; seen to be happening</li>
<li>MEASURABLE&gt; quantified in an objective way</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="components-criteria-of-behavioral-objective">Components/criteria of behavioral objective<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#components-criteria-of-behavioral-objective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>There are three parts of an objectives, namely:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>A verb</li>
<li>The condition under which the achievement will be demonstrated</li>
<li>The standard or criteria by which the performance will be evaluated</li>
</ol>
<ol>
<li>ACTION VERB ( act or performance)</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>It describes what the learner is expected to do.</li>
<li>It describes the specific behavior or activity of the learner</li>
<li>The student will be able to, list, describe, illustrate, demonstrate</li>
<li>The performance indicator is the act whose satisfactory performance implies that the student is able to accomplish the task required</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-the-condition">2. THE CONDITION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-the-condition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Describes how the learner is going to carry out the activity to behave in a specific manner under certain conditions.</li>
<li>The teacher should describe the situation or specific condition under which the learner is expected to carry out the activity</li>
<li>Eg giving immunization in MCH</li>
<li>It includes data, limitations &amp;restrictions</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>STANDARD/CRITERIA</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>This is the minimum acceptable accomplishment by the learner</li>
<li>Note that the learner may not perform the expected task at a maximum level but should acquire at least a certain amount of the total knowledge or skill taught to them</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assignment">ASSIGNMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assignment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>READ AND MAKE NOTES ON THE ADVANTAGES AND DISADVANTAGES OF OBJECTIVES</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="teaching-aids-instructional-media">TEACHING AIDS/ INSTRUCTIONAL MEDIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#teaching-aids-instructional-media" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>These are objects or situations which facilitate teaching/learning process and at the same time permits a teacher and learner to interact as much as possible.</li>
<li>The use of teaching aid simulates the learner through the following senses:</li>
<li>Sight</li>
<li>Hearing</li>
<li>Touch</li>
<li>Taste</li>
<li>smell</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-teaching-aid">Types of teaching aid<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-teaching-aid" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Categorized into 3</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Projected</li>
<li>Non projected</li>
<li>Sound</li>
</ol>
<table><thead><tr><th>PROJECTED</th><th>NON PROJECTED</th><th>SOUND</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>OVERHEAD PROJECTOR</td><td>FLIPCHARTS</td><td>RADIO</td></tr><tr><td>VIDEOS</td><td>FLANNEL BOARD</td><td>VIDEO</td></tr><tr><td>TELEVISION</td><td>PICTURES</td><td>TELEVISION</td></tr><tr><td>LED- POWERPOINT</td><td>POSTERS</td><td></td></tr><tr><td></td><td>WRITING BOARD</td><td></td></tr><tr><td></td><td>HAND OUTS</td><td></td></tr><tr><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="value-of-teaching-aid">VALUE OF TEACHING AID<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#value-of-teaching-aid" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Arouses interest</li>
<li>Time saving in teaching</li>
<li>Gives a new concept accurate impression</li>
<li>Stimulates active teaching provides a shared experience</li>
<li>Creates an opportunity for active learning</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="factors-influencing-selection-of-teaching-aids">Factors influencing selection of teaching aids<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-influencing-selection-of-teaching-aids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The subject matter</li>
<li>The objectives</li>
<li>The type of learning tasks ie skills, attitude, or knowledge</li>
<li>The learners background ie age, level of learning</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="categories-of-media">Categories of media<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#categories-of-media" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Visual- seeing</li>
<li>Audio- hearing</li>
<li>Audio-visual- seeing and visual</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="group-assignment">GROUP ASSIGNMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#group-assignment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>DISCUSS THE VARIOUS TYPES OF TEACHING AIDS, OUTLINING THE ADVANTAGES AND DISADVANTAGES</li>
</ul>
<p>a) Overhead projector</p>
<p>It projects transparencies from a horizontal table via a prism or mirror &amp; a lens</p>
<ul>
<li>A bright image appears on a screen behind the teacher</li>
<li>The setting up of the screen depends on the type of room &amp; the size of the audience.</li>
<li>There are two possibilities of projection:
a) projection from behind
b) projection slightly to the side (better viewing)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ohp-ct">OHP CT...<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ohp-ct" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>When lecturing, stand to the right or left of the projector so that you can easily point out the important areas that you want the learner to grasp.</li>
<li>You can also view what the learner is seeing simultaneously</li>
<li>Expose only what you are discussing &amp; not the whole transparency so that the learners can concentrate &amp; take down important points.</li>
<li>In this way, the rest of the presentation will not distract learners</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="when-preparing-transparencies">When preparing transparencies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#when-preparing-transparencies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Do not write too near the edge or you might lose half of the image; Leave at least an inch of margin all around.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>For more complex drawings, prepare a pencil sketch then lay the transparency over the sketch &amp; copy onto the transparency. You can also copy a diagram from a book.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lettering should not be too small, about 4mm(1/8 of an inch)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A transparency should convey one theme.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Put as much information as necessary but as little as possible on a transparency.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ensure clarity &amp; impact</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Leave room for future alterations.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Store your transparencies with care to avoid moisture &amp; dirt.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Keep content down to 10 lines with 10 words on each line.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When masking, use thin paper. This ensures that the lecturer sees the whole transparency but the audience only the information that has been revealed</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="advantages-of-ohp">Advantages of OHP<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-ohp" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>You are able to face the classroom &amp; point out features appearing on the screen easily using a pointer</li>
<li>It may not be necessary to darken the room</li>
<li>You are able to project a wide variety of materials.</li>
<li>Alternatively, they can be put up on top of each other showing stages of development of an idea or structure</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="disadvantages-of-using-an-ohp">Disadvantages of using an OHP<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages-of-using-an-ohp" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>The acetate sheets are expensive to obtain, but spoiled &amp; cleaned X-ray film is a useful alternative.</li>
<li>You should get a transparent &amp; slightly bluish sheet that can be used in the same way as transparent acetate sheets</li>
<li>Special felt pens are used for writing on the transparent sheets. If they are difficult to obtain, the glass pencils used in laboratories are a substitute.</li>
<li>Needs a lot of time 2 prepare &amp;Erase with water or with spirit for semi-permanent ink</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="care-and-maintenance-of-an-ohp">Care and Maintenance of an OHP<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#care-and-maintenance-of-an-ohp" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>After projection, do not remove the wire plug from the socket but switch off the lamp &amp; keep fan running until the bulb has cooled down.</li>
<li>Keep lenses &amp; mirrors free of dirt</li>
<li>Keep a spare bulb in stock at all times</li>
<li>Store semi-permanent transparencies together with master copies of handouts in a file with unit block or subject concerned, so it can be found easily &amp; used again the following year.</li>
</ul>
<p>B) LCD PROJECTOR AND LAPTOP</p>
<ul>
<li>In this system, content is typed in the power point in the computer &amp; projected onto a screen using the Liquefied crystal device (LCD) projector.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>NON-PROJECTED TEACHING AIDS</li>
</ol>
<p>These are aids that you can find within your environment</p>
<ul>
<li>You can select these well in advance of the lesson &amp; pre-test them before classroom use.</li>
</ul>
<p>These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>The chalkboard &amp; chalk/ white board &amp; marker</li>
<li>Pictures</li>
<li>Flipcharts/ charts</li>
<li>Posters</li>
<li>Handouts</li>
<li>flannel boards</li>
</ul>
<p>a) The chalk/white board</p>
<ul>
<li>These are the most easily available, convenient &amp; most used teaching aid</li>
</ul>
<p>Guidelines in using the chalkboard to enhance learning</p>
<ul>
<li>Write only the essential points &amp; examples e.g. your lesson plan outline.</li>
<li>This helps the learner copy &amp; fill in all other relevant information as you build up from introduction to conclusion.</li>
<li>Write large enough letters/figures to be seen by all learners.</li>
</ul>
<p>Ct...</p>
<ul>
<li>Plan the board so that information develops from one stage to the next stage.</li>
<li>Deliver the lecture to your audience &amp; not to the board, ie. if you have to write, lecture first, then write on the board.</li>
<li>Stand next to the board at an angle so that you can see your learners frequently.</li>
<li>Maintain eye contact with the class</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="advantages-of-chalk-white-boards">Advantages of chalk/white boards<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-chalk-white-boards" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Easy to use</li>
<li>Inexpensive</li>
<li>Excellent for brainstorming</li>
<li>Displays information</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="disadvantages">Disadvantages<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Time consuming</li>
<li>Messy</li>
<li>Cannot hold a large amount of information</li>
<li>No permanent record of information</li>
<li>Lecture maybe delivered to the board instead of the learners</li>
</ul>
<p>b) Pictures</p>
<ul>
<li>Can be in form of slides, photographs, picture-drawings, line drawings or cartoons</li>
<li>Good &amp; appropriate pictures are sometimes difficult to obtain or prepare</li>
</ul>
<p>C) Charts</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Are cheap &amp; easy aids to prepare</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Simple charts Can be made from butcher paper, old calendars, paper boxes, manila paper, etc</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Flip charts are commercial plain papers</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>-The pictures can be drawn by somebody else or traced from a book</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>-The pictures should be labeled in legible handwriting</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>-When labeling, remember to:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Use thick felt pens</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Use different colors for emphasis</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Write in lower case letters, not capitals</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Do not write too much / donâ€™t congest it</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When making a presentation using flipcharts, do not read the chart as you talk.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>As you prepare the lesson or the materials for teaching, make notes on your lesson plan to guide your discussion.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This way, you can read your notes as you teach &amp; yet be facing the audience</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="flipcharts">Flipcharts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#flipcharts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Large sheets of paper usually in a tripod stand</li>
<li>Used to display previously prepared notes or drawings</li>
<li>Also used for brainstorming or discussions</li>
<li>Advantages</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Inexpensive</li>
<li>Excellent for brainstorming</li>
<li>Portable</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="disadvantages-of-flipcharts">Disadvantages of flipcharts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages-of-flipcharts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Time consuming</li>
<li>Messy</li>
<li>Cannot hold a large amount of information</li>
</ol>
<p>d) Posters</p>
<p>They take longer to prepare than charts</p>
<ul>
<li>They may consist of words only, pictures only, or a mixture of both.</li>
<li>Unlike flipcharts, posters are usually single-leafed.</li>
<li>Posters need a lot of planning &amp; testing before use.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="posters-ct">Posters ct...<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#posters-ct" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>They can be prepared for two types of viewers:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>For a mixed (heterogeneous) audience eg. on a street for the public</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>In this case, it should deliver the message at a glance</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>For a captive audience, eg. in a class</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>NB: When preparing a poster, remember to make it simple, use simple language &amp; avoid difficult words or slang &amp; put as little as possible on the poster</li>
</ul>
<p>e) The real thing or object</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>It is the best teaching aid e.g. real baby instead of a doll</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Try as much as possible to use the â€˜real thingâ€™ in your lesson</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If it is not possible to demonstrate â€˜the real thingâ€™ think of other teaching aids that are simulations of the real thing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The closer the simulation to the real thing, the better the teaching aid is.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This helps the learner to internalize &amp; transfer the impression he gets to the real thing</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It also helps the learner to start using the right attitudes &amp; find the right expressions to use from the start.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>f) Handouts</p>
<ul>
<li>These are written papers given out by teachers to students</li>
<li>They act as guides for work to be done, or references to be looked up.</li>
<li>They help remind students of the main points to remember from a learning experience</li>
<li>They should not be used as substitutes for manuals, texts &amp; references</li>
<li>A handout is both a visual aid to learning &amp; an addition to private study.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="purpose-of-a-handout">Purpose of a handout<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#purpose-of-a-handout" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is to help the teacher to:</p>
<ol>
<li>Indicate the objectives of the lesson exercise</li>
<li>Indicate the relevance &amp; define the area to be covered</li>
<li>Provide additional theoretical information</li>
<li>Provide a stimulus for further thinking</li>
<li>Give instructions for practical work; these should be specific &amp; complete</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="uses-features-characteristics-of-a-good-handout">Uses/features/characteristics of a good handout<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uses-features-characteristics-of-a-good-handout" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-good-handout-should">A good handout should:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-good-handout-should" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Set out the structure of a lesson to promote attainment of the objectives</li>
<li>Benefit learning</li>
<li>Provide an infrastructure for the topic</li>
<li>Emphasize a framework for interaction between the facilitator &amp; learner</li>
<li>Help the learner to receive detailed information</li>
<li>Guarantee the accuracy of the transferred information</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="useful-guidelines-when-preparing-a-handout">Useful guidelines when preparing a handout<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#useful-guidelines-when-preparing-a-handout" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The introduction should relate the new material to the learnerâ€™s past experience</li>
<li>Summarize the major ideas</li>
<li>Use major &amp; minor topics</li>
<li>Leave space between paragraphs &amp; sections for learners to make notes</li>
<li>Simplify your expressions</li>
<li>Label your illustrations, tables &amp; graphs appropriately. A series of diagrams building up to a complete concept may be more helpful than one detailed diagram</li>
</ul>
<p>Put questions &amp; exercises within the text to stimulate thinking</p>
<p>âž¤ The content, language &amp; spelling should be accurate.</p>
<p>âž¤ The statements should be consistent with other texts or manuals which the learners use.</p>
<p>âž¤ Your handouts must be clear &amp; arranged in a logical order with good arrangement of headings, words &amp; diagrams on the page</p>
<p>g) Flannel board</p>
<ul>
<li>This is the device of choice for teaching villagers.</li>
<li>All rural educators should know how to use it</li>
<li>It is based on the fact that materials with rough surfaces tend to adhere to each other</li>
<li>If flannel cloth is not available, alternatives can be found.</li>
</ul>
<p>Ct...</p>
<ul>
<li>The board is put in front of the class, sloping slightly backwards</li>
<li>Cards with a rough backing eg. sand paper, can be placed on the board in the desired position.</li>
<li>The cards can be moved or taken down at will.</li>
<li>Make cards from large print or written words eg. newspaper cuttings, photographs or dissected posters</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="advantages-of-flannel-board">Advantages of flannel board<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-flannel-board" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>It tells a story in which you can see things happen</li>
<li>It has strong colors that please</li>
<li>The pictures are large enough to be seen from some way off.</li>
<li>It looks like things that people are familiar with</li>
<li>It arouses interest &amp; questions</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="disadvantages-of-flannel-board">Disadvantages of flannel board<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages-of-flannel-board" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Barazas are usually too big for flannel pictures to be seen from the back</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>when flannels are used in the open air, the wind may blow the flannel graphs away</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>NB: even the best designed teaching aid cannot replace practical work with patients &amp; in the community</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="how-to-use-teaching-aids">HOW TO USE TEACHING AIDS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-to-use-teaching-aids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Good use of teaching aids involve</li>
<li>Selecting</li>
<li>Previewing</li>
<li>Planning</li>
<li>Presenting</li>
<li>Evaluating</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="how-to-use-teaching-aids">How to use teaching aids<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-to-use-teaching-aids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<ol>
<li>Select: the teaching aids to suit the lesson</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="2">
<li>Preview the teaching aid to ensure they convey the message you want</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<p>Avoid unpleasant surprises</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>During the preview, plan explanations or comments you may wish to make during presentation of your lesson</p>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="3">
<li>Plan how and in what order you intend to use your teaching aid eg by numbering them</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<p>In the plan: introduce the subject in an interesting way, describe the body of the topic and then summarize the lesson to ensure consolidation of knowledge</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tell the learner what to look for as you explain and comment where necessary</p>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="4">
<li>Present: your teaching aid appropriately and give adequate explanation</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<p>The students view the teacher as an expert</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Check the mechanical equipment to ensure it is in good working condition</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If working in a community eg field trip, obtain consent from the persons involved</p>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="5">
<li>Evaluate: your teaching aids with the same class</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<p>After presenting your teaching aid, find out if the presentation was successful, whether the aid achieved its purpose and if the objective was attained</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="general-storage-of-teaching-aids">GENERAL STORAGE OF TEACHING AIDS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-storage-of-teaching-aids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Good durable teaching aids can be reused.</li>
<li>Keep your teaching aids neatly in a resource learning kit(cupboard/store)</li>
<li>Each item should be labeled clearly for easy access</li>
<li>Maintain an inventory of the various aids in stock</li>
<li>When you lend out items, they should be signed for.</li>
</ul>
<p>Storage ct...</p>
<ul>
<li>On their return, you should check their condition first before storing so that you keep readily usable items in your resource centre or cupboard</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="storage-of-specific-teaching-aids">Storage of specific teaching aids<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#storage-of-specific-teaching-aids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Maps &amp; charts are stored rolled up.</li>
<li>To avoid long searches, their titles should be written on the back &amp; facing the door so that they can be seen easily.</li>
<li>Slides are best kept in hanging files with a list of contents on the filing cabinet.</li>
<li>Overhead transparencies &amp; master copies of handouts are put in a master file together with other material on that special unit.</li>
</ul>
<p>The master copies are given numbers corresponding to the no. of stencils, which are stored in or near the stencil room</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>These are filed in either alphabetical order or numerically</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When a handout is needed, it is easy to trace back the old stencil &amp; run off the quantity needed.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Handouts need to be updated with current information.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Models, samples &amp; specimens may be kept for a permanent exhibit in the library.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assessment-and-evaluation">ASSESSMENT AND EVALUATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment-and-evaluation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Evaluation involves placing a value on the learnerâ€™s performance in order to make a decision about the learner&amp; the subject or course that was taught</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="components-of-evaluation">Components of Evaluation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#components-of-evaluation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-examination">a) Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Is the formal mechanism or process used to determine the degree of learning of the learner?</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="b-assessment">b) Assessment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Refers to the process of finding out to what extent the learner has achieved the set objectives</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="purpose-aims-significance-of-evaluation">PURPOSE/AIMS/SIGNIFICANCE OF EVALUATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#purpose-aims-significance-of-evaluation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>You should evaluate the learner in order to:</li>
<li>Help the learner to understand him/herself</li>
<li>Help in retention &amp; transfer of learning</li>
<li>Motivate the learner</li>
<li>Predict the level of learnersâ€™ future performance</li>
<li>Judge the learners achievements</li>
<li>Monitor the learners progress for the purpose of providing feedback</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; Determine teaching effectiveness
&gt; License practice of a profession
&gt; Identify weak &amp; strong areas of a course
&gt; Grade &amp; rank students
&gt; Gauge reputation of school performance
&gt; Protect society, ie, to inform the community of the extent to which graduates constitute a potential danger</p>
